  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2728690591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer325209652649487215">Excuse me as I wipe the tears from my eyes . . . . <br/><br/>This has become my number one favorite ( so far ) of the Ranger's Apprentice series and I doubt it will ever be overtaken. It showed immeasurable strength and advancement in its form and I appreciated all aspects of John Flanagan's workmanship. He's is certainly no beginner in the craft of tale weaving. It's marvellous, and it's homey. <br/><br/>I am struggling emotionally with the book because my ships aren't working out, but I refuse to demote it to 4 s</span>
  <span id="freeText325209652649487215" style="display:none">Excuse me as I wipe the tears from my eyes . . . . <br /><br />This has become my number one favorite ( so far ) of the Ranger's Apprentice series and I doubt it will ever be overtaken. It showed immeasurable strength and advancement in its form and I appreciated all aspects of John Flanagan's workmanship. He's is certainly no beginner in the craft of tale weaving. It's marvellous, and it's homey. <br /><br />I am struggling emotionally with the book because my ships aren't working out, but I refuse to demote it to 4 stars simply because of my disappointment. This adventure had me running and squealing around the room at the end of every ending chapters!! =) Its worthy of 5 stars. <br /><br />Oh and the characters?? Please. I will get to worked up talking about them. All you need to know is each character is crafted unique to him/her self and they come across crystal clear in their own ways. It's wonderful seeing them function together ( and fight!! ) and tease one another. I have a great deal of respect for John Flanagan, his characters do not make me cringe, scream in agony, or tap my fingers thinking how stupid or annoying that particular trait is. They all deserve perfect respect in the group and I admire ( love 💞 ) them all the same. <br /><br />What's the content, you ask?? It's a war!! In the desert!! With little water!! And merciless killers!! Get the picture?? Good. Now you can be happy. <br /><br />I don't have anything else to say. I'm grinning my face off. It's a good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="325209652649487215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140749243?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chichipio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chichipio" href="/user/show/1870710-chichipio">Chichipio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399252051" href="/book/show/6719735-erak-s-ransom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1870710-chichipio?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140749243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7557694567704032151">It would have worked great as a fifth book. As a seventh, however, loses major points. <br/><br/>First, you have to get over the fact that you won't get to know what happens after the end of book six for a while longer.<br/><br/>Then, once you start warming up to this story, you realize that there's no sense of urgency to it. It's not because any fault with the writing, but because you already know how things are going to turn up for the characters.<br/><br/>For example, at Tug's disappearance, nobody could have any doubts t</span>
  <span id="freeText7557694567704032151" style="display:none">It would have worked great as a fifth book. As a seventh, however, loses major points. <br /><br />First, you have to get over the fact that you won't get to know what happens after the end of book six for a while longer.<br /><br />Then, once you start warming up to this story, you realize that there's no sense of urgency to it. It's not because any fault with the writing, but because you already know how things are going to turn up for the characters.<br /><br />For example, at Tug's disappearance, nobody could have any doubts that the little horse would be all right since we already know he's with Will in books 5 and 6. Now, Tug is a secondary character, and his death could add a lot of drama and character development to the story, so imagine reading this as a fifth book… The uncertainty, the possibilities, the "would Flanagan really kill Tug?" kind of questions would have made for an amazing tension. As it is, knowing how things turn up, it felt a little flat.<br /><br />So, on its own, not a bad a read, certainly not the worst of the series by any means. But as a part of the whole, its misplacement in the timeline works against making it truly enjoyable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7557694567704032151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3751828819630676381" style="display:none">One of the best in the series, set in Arabian lands called Arridin and reminiscent at times of the movie <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/791946.Hidalgo_and_Other_Stories" title="Hidalgo and Other Stories by Frank T. <div id="review_282983738" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282983738" />
    <a title="Thais" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1400349-thais"><img alt="Thais" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282983738?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thais" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thais" href="/user/show/1400349-thais">Thais</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282983738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10190860648805368979">This was the first book in the series that I was disappointed in. If it had been placed in it's proper sequence according to the timeline of the other books, it would be read before book 5. Flanagan goes back in time to tell a story before Will becomes a full fledged Ranger. If it had been placed before book 5, I wouldn't have been disappointed. However, I felt that there were certain elements that would have been referred to in book 5 and 6 that couldn't because this book hadn't been written ye</span>
  <span id="freeText10190860648805368979" style="display:none">This was the first book in the series that I was disappointed in. If it had been placed in it's proper sequence according to the timeline of the other books, it would be read before book 5. Flanagan goes back in time to tell a story before Will becomes a full fledged Ranger. If it had been placed before book 5, I wouldn't have been disappointed. However, I felt that there were certain elements that would have been referred to in book 5 and 6 that couldn't because this book hadn't been written yet. I ended up feeling that books 5 and 6 couldn't be true to the same style of writing Flanagan usually uses to connect his stories because it wasn't possible. For example, this book starts off with slight jealousy from a female protaganist. However, this was not an interesting plot point because at the end of book 6, you know which female protaganist Will falls in love with. Flanagan says that he wanted to tell of the separation anxieties between teacher and student as Will approaches graduation. I agree that I wanted that to be part of the series. I was disappointed when book 4 jumped several years and skipped the rest of his apprentice days. However, because Will already proved his capabalities in book 5 and 6 there is less buy in when Will is wondering if he can survive in his own right as a full Ranger. You already know how he handles his first assignment before it has been given to him. I will still intend to finish the last of the series because I like the characters, but my enthusiasm has waned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10190860648805368979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

One of my favorites in the whole Ranger's Apprentice series <3 <br/>Erak's Ransom is: <br/>*Cute!   <span id="freeText14218014564896810780" style="display:none">Well well well, that went too well. It was fantastic in fact! One of my favorites in the whole Ranger's Apprentice series &lt;3 <br />Erak's Ransom is: <br />*Cute! (Halt's wedding, sweet remarks between Halt and Lady Pauline, Horace and Gilan, Will's graduation)<br />*Adventurous! (I just love how the adventures take place in different landscapes and countries: Celtica, Lands of Rain and Night, Skandia, Gallia, Arrida -I'm not sure the spelling is correct. The characters have experienced the freezing climate of Skandia, the savory Gallian coffee, the Arridi sandstorms and desserts. This all brings new experiences for both the characters and the readers who feel engaged in the series ^_^ )<br />*Excellent Narrative! (The best parts were when Halt was about to be executed and Will sent a hissing arrow at the executioner's chest, gluing him to the ground, and when Will received his Silver Oakleaf: how he was so dejected and disappointed at the extremely simple, almost dull course of his graduation ceremony, yet then all his friends and some other rangers yell a loud CONGRATULATIONS! <br />*Diversity of Characters: One of the basic reasons why I regretted Icebound Land was that it is a monotonous narrative of Will and Evanlyn's life in Skandia. Almost all characters appeared in Erak's Ransom along with new ones: King Duncan, Cassandra, Lord Anthony, Halt, Lady Pauline, Alyss, Jenny, George, Horace, Will, Gilan, Crowely, Sir Rodney, Umar, Selethen, Erak, Savengal, and many more. I realized that Gilan and Horace's presence was crucial in any book, for their extreme sweetness, light humor, and cheerful innocence were indispensable :D ) <br /><br />Erak's Ransom is a masterpiece, John Flanagan! I truly thank you! </span>

  <span id="freeText16623760020126698678" style="display:none">Okay, first, this book is non-chronological with the rest of the series so-far. it doesn't offer any spoilers or anything really of value where it is in sequence (out-of-chronology), so I'd suggest reading the books in this order (so far)<br /><br />1-2-3-4-7-5-6<br /><br />I'll edit my book 5 review to reflect that as well..<br /><br /><br />..anyway, I really liked this book as well. As I've said on all the other ones in this series, it's candy fiction. It's not deep, but it sure is fun. <br /><br />This one takes place in a north-africa-type setting. All the civilizations in this series are based on real historical ones. I've mentioned elsewhere that the merits of such a setting are debatable, but whatever.<br /><br />Anyways, it was a page turner. I found myself making excuses to return to the book throughout the day just to get another dose.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4986057443353817539">Will the Ranger meets Lawrence of Arabia, and a good time is had by all (well, except for a little being chained to camels and almost beheaded, etc)! No, not really Lawrence, but definitely Arabia, and the book is much the better for a little touch of exoticism and the lack of rain (I don't know why, but whenever I think of this series, I picture a guy with a longbow standing in drizzling rain). I got kind of tired of the series last year, but had a yen to pick it up again, and I'm glad I did. I</span>
  <span id="freeText4986057443353817539" style="display:none">Will the Ranger meets Lawrence of Arabia, and a good time is had by all (well, except for a little being chained to camels and almost beheaded, etc)! No, not really Lawrence, but definitely Arabia, and the book is much the better for a little touch of exoticism and the lack of rain (I don't know why, but whenever I think of this series, I picture a guy with a longbow standing in drizzling rain). I got kind of tired of the series last year, but had a yen to pick it up again, and I'm glad I did. It's not madly original or fabulously well-written, but it's a lot of fun--and it makes no claims to being madly original or profound, either, which is always nice.</span>

  <span id="freeText1694578571213649535" style="display:none">Well at first I planned to take away a star because this book is a prequel to The Sorcerer of the North, which is just like what?! Seriously?? I got over it pretty quickly, but still. I wish I could have read them in the right order instead of jumping back in the story like that. I decided to add the star back because, miracle of miracles! I finished the book and realized there was only like one cuss word in the whole thing!! It's a record for Ranger's Apprentice. I hope the rest of the books are the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1694578571213649535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer337739847785899645">Well...well... looks like Will &co. were loooong way from home in this 7th book... Get trapped on sand storm, lost direction and half dead on vast dessert, wagering Tug on Bedullin tribe's race and Halt nearly beheaded? What went wrong here? Wait a minute, where were they actually?<br/>(By the way, story wise it was between 4th and 5th book, so I read this before the 5th, but it was the 7th book of the installment) <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Taken time some years after the peace treaty had signed between Araluen</span></span>
  <span id="freeText337739847785899645" style="display:none">Well...well... looks like Will &amp;co. were loooong way from home in this 7th book... Get trapped on sand storm, lost direction and half dead on vast dessert, wagering Tug on Bedullin tribe's race and Halt nearly beheaded? What went wrong here? Wait a minute, where were they actually?<br />(By the way, story wise it was between 4th and 5th book, so I read this before the 5th, but it was the 7th book of the installment) <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Taken time some years after the peace treaty had signed between Araluen and Skandian, Svengal took a liberty to crashed at Halt and Pauline's wedding party, brought the news of Oberjarl Erak's hostage situation by the Arridis. Arrida is a dry land far south of Araluen, where the mainland's dessert still unknown to most outsiders. Considering Erak's position as leader of a nation, another monarch should attended this matter as the mediator, but as King Duncan was really occupied by something-something, Princess Cassandra volunteering on his behalf. So along with her, the King assigned Halt as her advisor, Will tagged along as her trusted companion and Horace was appointed as her personnal body guard. Gilan, who accidentally caught King's eyes along his cloak and sword, also dragged into. So all five of them, nine if we count the horses, -The Fellowship of The Rangers- accompanied Svegal back to Arrida to pay Erak's Ransom. <br /><br />In Arrida, Cassandra successfully arranged the ransom with Selethen, the Wakir, or Lord, of the teritory. But when they went to Mararoc to get Erak, everything crushed and crumbling down. Selethen's men slayed and Erak's gone. Latter, Halt and the others were captured by Tualaghi, who they called The Blue Veiled Ones, while Will, seperated from the rest, embarked on his own journey, a solo mission to find Tug, and to verify his own readiness of being a full flagged Ranger. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />***<br /><br />What I like of this series was -beside the truely entertaining tales- how it really emphasized of the 'growing up' process all the way of the story. Will was maturing in front our eyes. In the first book, we saw that little dubious boy, uncertain of his own feet and eyes. Then he change into a worthy ranger apprentice. In second book we saw him so groggy in front of his first real combat. Latter we saw his unwavering will to burn a bridge, not even blinking his eye in the face of ample enemies. So was in the forth book, where he change again from a mere apprentice into a prominent leader of one extraordinary courageous troop. Now as he's about to enter his adultness, he was questioning his own ability to coupe with life. Something that I thought, one time of another, we question ourselves too. And in the end, life did came whether he's ready or not. But with his band of friends and mentors cheering and pretty ladies in both arms, being adult was not so bad after all. *or so you said, wait until these ladies had a cat fight, and then you wished you just a simple boy running away after stealing food from mr. chubbs* :D<br /><br />#28/2013</span>

<div id="review_606461704" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606461704" />
    <a title="Gillian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3614402-gillian"><img alt="Gillian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423020250p2/3614402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/606461704?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gillian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gillian" href="/user/show/3614402-gillian">Gillian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399252051" href="/book/show/6719735-erak-s-ransom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3614402-gillian?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer606461704&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer606461704" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12098010146536024342">Another strong addition to the <i>Ranger's Apprentice</i> series!<br/><br/>Look, I literally cannot dislike these books, you guys. These books are like junk food. Sometimes I just feel like reading heroic tales about knights and princesses and kingdoms and all that, okay? And this book series always delivers.<br/><br/>But anyway, this particular book was interesting for many reasons. For one, it takes place chronologically before Book six, which I found a little jarring, especially since I had literally just finished book</span>
  <span id="freeText12098010146536024342" style="display:none">Another strong addition to the <i>Ranger's Apprentice</i> series!<br /><br />Look, I literally cannot dislike these books, you guys. These books are like junk food. Sometimes I just feel like reading heroic tales about knights and princesses and kingdoms and all that, okay? And this book series always delivers.<br /><br />But anyway, this particular book was interesting for many reasons. For one, it takes place chronologically before Book six, which I found a little jarring, especially since I had literally just finished book six when I started this one. Still, it isn't confusing. I did feel like a bit of character development had been lost, which of course is to be expected, but still, compared to book six, the characters seemed flatter.<br /><br />Other than that, though, the other interesting part of this book was the exotic setting! Yes, that's right, no longer are our heroes fighting evil in Araluen! Nope, they've found themselves in an Arabian-esque location, facing heat, blazing sun, lack of water, and camels!<br /><br />I loved the world-building that happened in this book. The world of <i>Ranger's Apprentice</i> is so rich and full of culture, and this just added on to it. <br /><br />Flanagan did a great job at putting me on the edge of my seat and making me feel the emotions in the book. Especially when Will lost Tug. I was for serious about to burst into tears until I realized that Tug shows up in book six, which happens after book seven, and then my faith in Will was restored.<br /><br />Another thing I quite liked in this book was the return of Evanlyn! She's back! And just as much of a BAMF as before. This time, however, she shows off her princess-ly duties and is basically an amazing negotiator. However, the return of Evanlyn also brought up some rivalry between her and Alyss which... I felt was a little out of the blue? I guess we hadn't really seen any actual interactions between Alyss and Evanlyn before, so there was no way to really know if they'd have a rivalry, but I don't know... it just seemed forced? Both girls seemed out of character in the few scenes that it focused on their rivalry over Will. It just bothered me.<br /><br />Halt's back too! I missed him more than I knew last book! I loved the expansion on his relationship with Will. Gilan too, whom I forgot that I loved so much.<br /><br />So, tl;dr, I liked this book. It was a change of pace from it's predecessors, if not a little jarring. Although I liked the return of many of the characters, Alyss and Evanlyn's rivalry seemed forced and kind of out of character for both of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12098010146536024342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289598-marjolein?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289598-marjolein?shelf=children-ya">children-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289598-marjolein?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer372274707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14412848281210746680">3.5 stars<br/><br/><i> Read all my reviews on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com'>http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com</a> </i><br/><br/>It has been a year since I read the sixth book in the Ranger's Apprentice series and since I was looking for an Australian author to read for the Southern Hemisphere reading challenge, it seemed the perfect moment to pick this series up.<br/><br/>For this book I've made the change from reading it in Dutch, to English. This caused little problems (it took me quite some time to realize that Horace is Arnaut from the Dutch books), but after</span>
  <span id="freeText14412848281210746680" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br /><i> Read all my reviews on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com">http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com</a> </i><br /><br />It has been a year since I read the sixth book in the Ranger's Apprentice series and since I was looking for an Australian author to read for the Southern Hemisphere reading challenge, it seemed the perfect moment to pick this series up.<br /><br />For this book I've made the change from reading it in Dutch, to English. This caused little problems (it took me quite some time to realize that Horace is Arnaut from the Dutch books), but after some initial confusion it was a good read.<br /><br />Because of the time between the books, I wasn't bothered too much with the weird chronology in this part of the series (book 7 takes place before books 5 and 6). Apparently, John Flanagan decided he had left out some of Will's story and just added it later.<br /><br />So, Erak's Ransom takes place just before Will becomes a real Ranger, and he will need everything he has learned when they venture into the desert to save an old friend, Erak, who's been captured.<br /><br />I quite liked the story of this one. I felt that, compared for example with book six, more things happened and there was more suspense (though it was limited a little bit with the fact that this book takes place earlier). Will however annoyed me a little as he is turning more and more in the special snowflake one who is the only one who can solve things and is also the one who is always right. I like my main characters slightly more flawed.<br /><br />Looking forward to the next book!</span>

<div id="review_110061331" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110061331" />
    <a title="Loralee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3169163-loralee"><img alt="Loralee" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110061331?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Loralee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Loralee" href="/user/show/3169163-loralee">Loralee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110061331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1170785730326431574">It's not <i>To Kill a Mockingbird</i> or <i>Lord of the Rings.</i> But for what this book is supposed to be, a YA fantasy novel, it's brilliantly put together. Good sound plot, memorable characters, satisfying action scenes, near-death in the desert, traitors, bargaining, horse-racing, archery, and a princess with a sharp turn for bargaining--as well as a mean slingshot. The quality of this novel is even more remarkable considering this is the seventh book in the series, although the author has wisely tackled</span>
  <span id="freeText1170785730326431574" style="display:none">It's not <i>To Kill a Mockingbird</i> or <i>Lord of the Rings.</i> But for what this book is supposed to be, a YA fantasy novel, it's brilliantly put together. Good sound plot, memorable characters, satisfying action scenes, near-death in the desert, traitors, bargaining, horse-racing, archery, and a princess with a sharp turn for bargaining--as well as a mean slingshot. The quality of this novel is even more remarkable considering this is the seventh book in the series, although the author has wisely tackled story lines in single books or pairs, not tried to carry a single plot throughout. In fact, this book is set at an earlier time than the previous two, which is problematic only because you know the main characters must have survived. If you're not into swordfighting fantasy books for younger readers you might not enjoy it, but if you're interested in well-written, engaging fantasy that several of my young friends are reading, this is a great series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1170785730326431574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5080576931038508452" style="display:none">I love the ranger's apprentice series. But for the last few books I haven't really been feeling it, where the plot was going. <br /><br />This goes back in time in comparison to the last two books by being in the time period when Will is still an apprentice. I thought that this bridged the gap nicely and I am ready for the next one in the series. <br /><br />The characters are much the same as they have been before, and it seems that all the actions are kind of shallow. But Will goes through some really trying times. Though the suspense of the book was not too much, since the whole time I was thinking they can't kill him off, he was in <br />the last book! There are also many of the best character in this book, sort of like a celebrity version of it. But that makes it so that many times you forget they're there and they fade into the background, if you don't remember they're there, they're not important enough, and you don't care about them. I really wish I'd cared about them. <br /><br />I think if John Flanagan had released this book before the last two it would have been more exiting to read. But I'm just glad he released it. </span>

<div id="review_107727297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107727297" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107727297?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/32954930-erak-s-ransom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107727297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer395724410668321771">Well, as I've said before, this series of "YA" books has (in my opinion) run hot and cold. I found I lost interest during the volumes on the, The Icebound Land, and Oakleaf Bearers (though Oakleaf Bearers picks up a little in the4 end). This book hit me somewhat the same as these two. <br/><br/>First, this is a flashback...and with a "flashback in the center of a book series", I've always got to ask, "why"? The author says it's a sort of, an "oops, I forgot to tell you this story of what happened that led</span>
  <span id="freeText395724410668321771" style="display:none">Well, as I've said before, this series of "YA" books has (in my opinion) run hot and cold. I found I lost interest during the volumes on the, The Icebound Land, and Oakleaf Bearers (though Oakleaf Bearers picks up a little in the4 end). This book hit me somewhat the same as these two. <br /><br />First, this is a flashback...and with a "flashback in the center of a book series", I've always got to ask, "why"? The author says it's a sort of, an "oops, I forgot to tell you this story of what happened that led up to Will's promotion to full Ranger-hood". Okay...I guess, but not it's not like the story (at least seems) to be that important to the overall tale. Then again I know it's a youth book and just the "having of another story" will be greatly pleasing to some. So, enjoy. <br /><br />I found that in the central portion of the book my interest began to wain and it kept fading in and out throughout the rest of that section... It was often I'd find my mind wandering and then have to "snap it back" sort of saying "oh, ya the book". That being said, let me say though that the book does pick back up and then runs to a nice climax and a satisfying (even slightly humorous) ending. I'm going with 3 stars here...it's close, but I believe that going to 4 will water down the rating for other 4 star books (including others in this series). 4 stars is a rating reserved for very good books that fall just short of the "huge" enjoyment or excellence offered by five star books...so, 3 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="395724410668321771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8007268398902909139">I deeply cherish these characters. I loved seeing each characters result of hard work and talent towards their profession. I’m glad to have read more of previous friendship between the Araluens and Skandians, with their still lasting bond for one another, despite the different upbringings, difficulties, and odds. I loved reading of Evanlyn’s authority and power, something that was not as easily shown in the previous books. I loved reading of Will accepting his fate, Halt’s creeping sorrow at los</span>
  <span id="freeText8007268398902909139" style="display:none">I deeply cherish these characters. I loved seeing each characters result of hard work and talent towards their profession. I’m glad to have read more of previous friendship between the Araluens and Skandians, with their still lasting bond for one another, despite the different upbringings, difficulties, and odds. I loved reading of Evanlyn’s authority and power, something that was not as easily shown in the previous books. I loved reading of Will accepting his fate, Halt’s creeping sorrow at losing his beloved apprentice, Alyss’ contribution and jealousy, King Duncan’s pure love for his daughter, and good Erak and Svengal, always there to make us laugh. <br /> And although I enjoyed this book, it’s placement in the series as the seventh book greatly demolished the tension and uncertainty. If it had been placed earlier in the series, it would have done a magnificent job of guaranteeing that I would not be able to put the book down, but as it was, I already knew the ending. I knew the plot. There was no urgency for me to finish, as I already knew it all. <br /> But, I loved the introduction to new characters and seeing previous enemies unite together to defeat a greater foe, resulting in lasting bonds and friendship. <br /> These characters, their story, bonds, and friendship will always have a place in my heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8007268398902909139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3292879824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3292879824" />
    <a title="Mara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73793647-mara"><img alt="Mara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515879322p2/73793647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3292879824?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/73793647-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/39918840-erak-s-ransom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73793647-mara?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73793647-mara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73793647-mara?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73793647-mara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73793647-mara?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3292879824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8216619150962563315">4/5 stars<br/><br/>I feel like I'm nitpicking, but I don't think that Flanagan is really good at describing relationships. Romantic ones, that is. He also suffers from the 'everyone has to be paired up syndrome'. I was shocked at the start of the book that <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Halt was marrying Lady Pauline  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It felt completely out of nowhere, and while the author mentioned that they had been seeking each other's company, it still felt really sudden. Not to mention that personally, I thought th</span>
  <span id="freeText8216619150962563315" style="display:none">4/5 stars<br /><br />I feel like I'm nitpicking, but I don't think that Flanagan is really good at describing relationships. Romantic ones, that is. He also suffers from the 'everyone has to be paired up syndrome'. I was shocked at the start of the book that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Halt was marrying Lady Pauline  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It felt completely out of nowhere, and while the author mentioned that they had been seeking each other's company, it still felt really sudden. Not to mention that personally, I thought that the two characters had not really much chemistry together, and after the story introduction, their relationship was thrown aside in favour of the ploy. It added no significance to the story, in my opinion. Additionally, I get tired to have Alyss and Will's 'relationship' shoved down my throat in an 'I tell you they like each other' way. Show, don't tell, and the author isn't really showing much of their relationship. The two barely have interactions and Will rarely thinks about her. And this is a relationship five years in the working??? Will thinks more often about Horace and Evanlyn than Alyss. Anyway, here is a quick breakdown of Alyss' appearances:<br /><br /><b>The Ruins of Gorlan:</b> she was there at the beginning (with all the other orphans), at a point in the middle of the story where all the orphans reunite and at the end. Where she suddenly kissed Will. It's isn't explained and only acknowledged once. <br /><b>The Burning Bridge:</b> Will thinks about Alyss at the very beginning and the kiss. Halt spends two chapters with Alyss and that is clearly from Halt's POV. Alyss isn't mentioned from chapter thirteen onward (40% into the book)<br /><b>The Icebound Lands:</b> Not mentioned at all<br /><b>The Battle for Skandia: </b> Not mentioned at all<br /><b>Erak's Ransom:</b> It starts of well. Alyss is the maid of honour, I think? She and Will are automatically paired up since Jenny immediately lusts after Gillan. (The: everyone has to be paired up syndrome) Also, Jenny has nothing to do <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ with Lady Pauline? Like, doesn't Pauline haven't any other apprentices/ex-apprentices she could have chosen?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Then you hear Alyss being jealous about Evanlyn as the crew rides off. In chapter fourteen (25% into the book) Will thinks about her <i>once</i>. Then she shows up in the epilogue again. <br /><br />I just don't get how we're supposed to root for these two when Will literally never thinks about her. I think Tug has shown up more than Alyss, and he is a pony. I'm not saying that they shouldn't end up together, but I want them to actually fall in love on-page. The only love interest that gets quite some page time is Evanlyn, and it's clear that she and Will aren't end game. Also, these characters are twenty??? Maybe nineteen, but still. They don't act like they have matured a lot, aside from Horace maybe. And of course, the only real female interaction we have (Evanlyn and Alyss) is pitty rivalry because both want to have Will? I still enjoy this man's books, but I definitely don't have to read them for romantic relationships or even the characters. I think this man's strength lies in putting together an interesting plot, an interesting setting and engaging and smart battles.<br /><br />The story itself, I really enjoyed. It was a fast-paced romp through the desert. I really liked the setting, how they had to deal with the trials of the desert and how out of depth the characters were. I thought that the battles were engaging and how the different elements came together. I thought especially the horse race was exciting. I like the large cast of characters, though I occasionally forgot somewhere there. Especially Svengal and Horace and at times even Gillan. Evanlyn was hard to forget because she was the only female in the group. And finally, Will went off on his own adventure, doing his own things without having Halt to guide him. I think it was an important part of his development, to see that he was 'ready' to become a Ranger. He still made mistakes, mistakes that almost got him killed, but as he survived, he showed strength. He remained cool in his attempt to get Tug back, won the trust of strangers and managed to come up with a plan to free his friends. He finally just got the chance to shine. <br /><br />While I enjoyed most of the story, it was the ending that got me weeping. It was rewarding to see how far Will had gotten over the course of the books. I still had wished that this was the end of the series, that all 10 books were about young Will, but I am curious to see what older Will will offer me. Also, I keep on saying this, I really like John Keating as an audiobook narrator. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8216619150962563315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3064707512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3064707512" />
    <a title="Stacy Fazenbaker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58640106-stacy-fazenbaker"><img alt="Stacy Fazenbaker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471201689p2/58640106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3064707512?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy Fazenbaker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy Fazenbaker" href="/user/show/58640106-stacy-fazenbaker">Stacy Fazenbaker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3064707512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2628772521291744475">“Always expect something to go wrong," he told him. "Believe me, if you're wrong, you're not dissapointed. If you're right, you're ready for it.”<br/>― John Flanagan, Erak's Ransom<br/><br/>Book 7 of the Ranger's Apprentice Series!! I have made it through book 7 already and the series is still fantastic and entertaining. This book was actually somewhat a prequel. It takes place before book 5 and 6. Flanagan felt like he rushed into Will being out on his own and he needed to go back and tell some of the story o</span>
  <span id="freeText2628772521291744475" style="display:none">“Always expect something to go wrong," he told him. "Believe me, if you're wrong, you're not dissapointed. If you're right, you're ready for it.”<br />― John Flanagan, Erak's Ransom<br /><br />Book 7 of the Ranger's Apprentice Series!! I have made it through book 7 already and the series is still fantastic and entertaining. This book was actually somewhat a prequel. It takes place before book 5 and 6. Flanagan felt like he rushed into Will being out on his own and he needed to go back and tell some of the story of the time leading up to Will becoming a full fledged ranger. I read a few reviews where people were upset that the story went backwards, but I enjoyed the additional story from that time frame. The only thing I would have changed is that I knew the fate of some of the characters beforehand because I have read the books that have a timeline later in Will's life. <br /><br />Erak's Ransom takes place a bit earlier in the timeline. Oberjarl Erak has been kidnapped and Will and all of his friends have been tasked to try and save him from his captors. Earlier in the series Erak and Will became friends despite their different backgrounds and lifestyles. Will immediately decided to go and help him, before his superiors told him he was going. I really enjoyed the adventure in this book and seeing how the events unfolded as the characters explored lands that they had never seen before. Book 7 added some great content about Will and how he was nervous and doubting himself as the time grew closer to him taking that final test to become a Ranger. <br /><br />I gave Erak's Ransom 4 stars as I have many of the others in this series. I didn't mind that the story was out of order as some did. Overall the series is fantastic and I highly recommend it. It is a young adult series so the reads are quick, but even as an adult the story is captivating and interesting throughout. I hope you enjoy as much as I have!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2628772521291744475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2033318862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2033318862" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/737152-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591837102p2/737152.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2033318862?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/737152-irene">Irene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399252051" href="/book/show/6719735-erak-s-ransom">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Upper elementary and middle school readers; fans of fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/737152-irene?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2033318862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer949758364040721223">Oh, I liked this book quite a bit! My 5th grader and I read it as a read-aloud, maybe that added to my enjoyment. <br/><br/>I was tipped off by other readers that this book - Book 7 - actually chronologically follows Book 4. It says as much in the Author's Note, but you'd never know if you were just reading them in order! <br/><br/>Well, not to give anything away, but I loved the beginning, which delved into the personal developments in the lives of some of the main characters. The overarching theme is that Will is</span>
  <span id="freeText949758364040721223" style="display:none">Oh, I liked this book quite a bit! My 5th grader and I read it as a read-aloud, maybe that added to my enjoyment. <br /><br />I was tipped off by other readers that this book - Book 7 - actually chronologically follows Book 4. It says as much in the Author's Note, but you'd never know if you were just reading them in order! <br /><br />Well, not to give anything away, but I loved the beginning, which delved into the personal developments in the lives of some of the main characters. The overarching theme is that Will is on the verge of becoming a full-fledged Ranger, and even though he's just about completed his apprenticeship, he doesn't feel like he's really ready to be on his own. <br /><br />By now, I'm liking the idea of meeting new peoples in different parts of this world. In this installment, we meet the Arridi (reminiscent of an Arabian culture) and the Bedullin (like Bedouins). There's a bit of international intrigue here, and it's fun to see where alliances lie. <br /><br />There were almost "too many" characters caught up in the main events, so frequently I'd even forget that Horace or Gilan were there, too. But that's okay. It was nice to see the whole gang together, even though they were facing danger. And I will say that even though I waver in my feelings towards Cassandra / Evanlyn, she did hold her own in this book. <br /><br />As usual, I really enjoyed the author's chuckle-worthy humor!</span>
  <a data-text-id="949758364040721223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_33413204'>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3QlCwNgG4lPI4EWJAuM3MtlZ5uqLtC8RPd/v8Sk0FrLnLysSY1grO2/L8ej1Fj3tDwYBIkU5oXZmoalA5HfkKA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GNcTYvvlofRD8LUsVo9zpMjlGwqnD7AveqKXbqRgr5Ai8XqwQLtonOTbAU2henl7Hrr8wmmCPkgh3NHfaSNdCg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText15409083837215535447" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /><br />For mysteries by this same author, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8307827.John_A__Flanagan" title="John A. Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">John A. Flanagan</a>.<br /><br />John Flanagan grew up in Sydney, Australia, hoping to be a writer. It wasn't until he wrote a highly uncomplimentary poem about a senior executive at the agency where he worked, however, that his talent was revealed. It turned out one of the company directors agreed with John's assessment of the executive, and happily agreed to train John in copywriting. <br /><br />After writing advertising copy for the next two decades, John teamed with an old friend to develop a television sitcom, Hey Dad!, which went on to air for eight years. <br /><br />John began writing Ranger's Apprentice for his son, Michael, ten years ago, and is still hard at work on the series. <br /><br />He currently lives in a suburb of Manly, Australia, with his wife. In addition to their son, they have two grown daughters and four grandsons.</span>

            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_11309018').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
